  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c2184915-d1d7-421e-b3e5-77d4842ac2f0'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer4892447234246844646">One Man Who Dared to Stand Up<br/><br/>Months of solitary confinement, years of periodic physical torture, constant suffering from hunger and cold, the anguish of brainwashing and mental cruelty—these are the experiences of a Romanian pastor during his 14 years in Communist prisons.<br/><br/>His crime, like that of thousands of others, was his fervant belief in Jesus Christ and his public wit</span>
  <span id="freeText4892447234246844646" style="display:none">One Man Who Dared to Stand Up<br /><br />Months of solitary confinement, years of periodic physical torture, constant suffering from hunger and cold, the anguish of brainwashing and mental cruelty—these are the experiences of a Romanian pastor during his 14 years in Communist prisons.<br /><br />His crime, like that of thousands of others, was his fervant belief in Jesus Christ and his public witness concerning that faith.<br /><br />Meeting in homes, in basements, and in woods—sometimes daring to preach in public on street corners—these faithful souls persisted in their Christian witness knowing full well the ultimate cost of their actions.<br /><br />This is their story—a classic account of courage, tenacious faith, and unbelievable endurance. This history of the Underground Church reflects the continuing struggle in many parts of the world today.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer29048413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12585285306020047261">Sitting in the balcony of my house in Egypt, I was reading this book with tears running down my cheek. Why would people have to live the story of the cross even though it is 2000 years after the event of Christ? As a Muslim then I reasoned that Christ must have been indeed crucified, contrary to what the Quran is stating. That book has helped me believe that the story of Christ in the gospel is real and not false as Islam claims. The sufferings of God's saints has confirmed to me that Christ rea</span>
  <span id="freeText12585285306020047261" style="display:none">Sitting in the balcony of my house in Egypt, I was reading this book with tears running down my cheek. Why would people have to live the story of the cross even though it is 2000 years after the event of Christ? As a Muslim then I reasoned that Christ must have been indeed crucified, contrary to what the Quran is stating. That book has helped me believe that the story of Christ in the gospel is real and not false as Islam claims. The sufferings of God's saints has confirmed to me that Christ really suffered before. He is the Lamb of God that was slain before the foundation of the world, and he is today slain the sufferings of His saints who joyfully count it worthy to suffer shame for his name's sake and say with the blessed Paul, With Christ I have been crucified, no longer do I live but Christ lives in me. By the way, please take a moment to read my story of conversion into Christianity and drop me a line and I will be your friend:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.answering-islam.org/authors/abraham/testimony.html">http://www.answering-islam.org/author...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12585285306020047261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1608709599" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1608709599" />
    <a title="Natalie Vellacott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34178791-natalie-vellacott"><img alt="Natalie Vellacott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442984500p2/34178791.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1608709599?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Vellacott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Vellacott" href="/user/show/34178791-natalie-vellacott">Natalie Vellacott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34178791-natalie-vellacott?shelf=christian-biography">christian-biography</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34178791-natalie-vellacott?shelf=christian-persecution">christian-persecution</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1608709599" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10514623324021636654">This is a short biographical account of a Romanian Pastor imprisoned and tortured for his Christian faith by the Communists just after the second world war. He spent a total of 14 years in prison, was eventually ransomed and released and moved to the West to encourage others to support "The Underground (persecuted) Church" in many countries. He founded "Voice of the Martyrs," which continues to work in countries around the world to this day.<br/><br/>Although the author states that he cannot go into graph</span>
  <span id="freeText10514623324021636654" style="display:none">This is a short biographical account of a Romanian Pastor imprisoned and tortured for his Christian faith by the Communists just after the second world war. He spent a total of 14 years in prison, was eventually ransomed and released and moved to the West to encourage others to support "The Underground (persecuted) Church" in many countries. He founded "Voice of the Martyrs," which continues to work in countries around the world to this day.<br /><br />Although the author states that he cannot go into graphic detail about the torture he endured at the hands of evil men. He proceeds to give seriously disturbing detail which some readers may not appreciate. He was placed in solitary confinement for 3 years!<br /><br /><i>"In solitary confinement, we could not pray as before. We were unimaginably hungry; we had been drugged until we acted like idiots. We were as weak as skeletons. The Lord's prayer was much too long for us- we could not concentrate enough to say it. My only prayer repeated again and again was, "Jesus, I love You."</i><br /><br />Personally I felt challenged when reading this and forced to ask myself questions about how far I would be willing to go for my Christian faith. The detail is not in any way included for entertainment or to assist the author in obtaining spiritual one-up-man-ship. I believe the author's main purpose in writing these things was to try and shock people into doing something to help the persecuted church. His passion, dedication and commitment to the cause resonate throughout the book and are compelling. Many Christian's have been and will continue to be seriously convicted about their own roles in this Gospel and help ministry to those that are suffering for Christ, this can only be a good thing. <br /><br />I note the complaints in various reviews about the author's negative/judgemental comments about Western Christian's. His attitude is that they are unconcerned, indifferent, apathetic and lacking in prayer for their brethren in crisis in other parts of the world. One reviewer's response which I would echo is that when reading/hearing criticism of ourselves we should examine (through Scripture and prayer) whether the things that are being said are true. If they are we should seek to address them and if they are not we should disregard them. Wurmbrand's opinion about Western Christian's may or may not be accurate, (in my view it is pretty accurate and has become more so in recent decades as this book was written a long time ago.) But, we cannot disregard his experiences and fail to help the persecuted church based on our prejudice towards him as an individual and how he chose to express himself. The things he experienced are happening around the world and the underground church does need help.<br /><br />To those that don't believe the content of the book (which I also read in some reviews.) I can understand the skepticism due to various Christian Biographical books being removed from sale due to the "made-up" stories. Wurmbrand has on his body the scars from the torture he endured at the hands of his persecutors as he revealed this during a public meeting. Again I believe he did this to capture the attention of people rather than for personal gain.<br /><br />I tend to believe the content of this book and that the author (who has since died) was a sincere soul seeking to follow Jesus and being willing to give up everything for that call. Ultimately only God knows his heart but we can all be challenged by his story and encouraged to get more involved in helping those suffering persecution in any way that we can.<br /><br />I would encourage adult Christians to read this book.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10514623324021636654" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15370465064405165996" style="display:none">This book isn't supposed to be a classic novel. It's not supposed to be poetic. It's not fictionalized into a drama, so what? <br /><br />This is one of the most powerful books I have ever read. Too many of us turn blind eyes to what our own government supports. Our policies support or install the dictators who torture people for their faith. Christians in the West must hold their leaders accountable or the evil experienced in the prisons of the USSR will continue. <br /><br />This is a very emotional, moving book that is a must read for anybody who is a Christian or thinks Communism is a good idea. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8876465391454360332">Excellent read.<br/><br/>I got <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18364928.Tortured_For_Christ' title='Tortured For Christ by Richard Wurmbrand' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tortured For Christ</a> for Free from The Voice of the Martyrs website: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://secure.persecution.com/referafriend/default.aspx?source=WEB'>https://secure.persecution.com/refera...</a> order yours if you want.<br/><br/>As I got this book I said why not get into the story and read it. I would recommend <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18364928.Tortured_For_Christ' title='Tortured For Christ by Richard Wurmbrand' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tortured For Christ</a> to all believers, even nonbelievers, who may have a change of heart after they've re</span>
  <span id="freeText8876465391454360332" style="display:none">Excellent read.<br /><br />I got <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18364928.Tortured_For_Christ" title="Tortured For Christ by Richard Wurmbrand" rel="nofollow noopener">Tortured For Christ</a> for Free from The Voice of the Martyrs website: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://secure.persecution.com/referafriend/default.aspx?source=WEB">https://secure.persecution.com/refera...</a> order yours if you want.<br /><br />As I got this book I said why not get into the story and read it. I will say that it is an incredible true story. This book should be required reading for all students. The human heart is capable of such evil and such good. I would recommend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18364928.Tortured_For_Christ" title="Tortured For Christ by Richard Wurmbrand" rel="nofollow noopener">Tortured For Christ</a> to all believers, even nonbelievers, who may have a change of heart after they've read this story. The book puts suffering for Christ into perspective and gives a call to action on helping persecuted Christians around the world.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8876465391454360332" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1555003732" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4956958785092069807">Wow.<br/><br/>What a book.<br/><br/>This book rendered my thoughts speechless multiple times as I was brought to consider how much Christians suffered for the sake of Christ under the Soviet Union and yet how much their joy and hope abounded throughout these dark times. Richard Wurmbrand and the other Christians who suffered certainly bore witness to Christ as they showed the exceeding power of Christ's unquenchable love and its ability to transform lives.<br/><br/>I was particularly struck by Wurmbrand's one plea to America</span>
  <span id="freeText4956958785092069807" style="display:none">Wow.<br /><br />What a book.<br /><br />This book rendered my thoughts speechless multiple times as I was brought to consider how much Christians suffered for the sake of Christ under the Soviet Union and yet how much their joy and hope abounded throughout these dark times. Richard Wurmbrand and the other Christians who suffered certainly bore witness to Christ as they showed the exceeding power of Christ's unquenchable love and its ability to transform lives.<br /><br />I was particularly struck by Wurmbrand's one plea to Americans: he and the other persecuted Christians didn't want to be rescued from Soviet Russia. They were all ready and willing to suffer for the sake of Christ if by doing so they could win others to him. All they needed from us were the resources and Bibles to use in order to win more to him.<br /><br />The faith and determination of Wurmbrand and these other believers impressed upon me again the all-worthiness and all-sufficiency of Christ. These believers saw Christ with eyes of faith that I can only hope to possess as well. The Holy Spirit truly is sufficient to take even the weakest believer and allow him to stand securely in faith. May we all look to have a faith like the faith of Wurmbrand and the other persecuted Christians by looking beyond them to the God whom they served.<br /><br />Rating: 5 Stars (Extremely Good).</span>

    <a title="Adam Parker" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4876781-adam-parker"><img alt="Adam Parker" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581994345p2/4876781.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/346916362?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adam Parker" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adam Parker" href="/user/show/4876781-adam-parker">Adam Parker</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4876781-adam-parker?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer346916362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14794400454448198744">... This book, more than any other up to this point, has left me speechless and caused much contimplation. Richard, in his simple writing style unadorned with trimmings, revealed a love I've not observed since the story of Jesus. The degree of suffering these men and women, fellow followers of Christ, suffered for "crimes" such as spreading gospel tracts or telling their children about God, is nearly beyond understanding. What IS beyond understanding though (outside of Jesus) is the unquenching,</span>
  <span id="freeText14794400454448198744" style="display:none">... This book, more than any other up to this point, has left me speechless and caused much contimplation. Richard, in his simple writing style unadorned with trimmings, revealed a love I've not observed since the story of Jesus. The degree of suffering these men and women, fellow followers of Christ, suffered for "crimes" such as spreading gospel tracts or telling their children about God, is nearly beyond understanding. What IS beyond understanding though (outside of Jesus) is the unquenching, unyielding, unrelenting genuine love these believers held for their captors. In spite of watching their children being literally whipped to death before their eyes, being fed endless amounts of salt without water until death, or being abducted and raped on their very wedding day, these lovers of Jesus remained lovers of those who hurt them, turning countless numbers of them to the love of Christ. <br /><br />This story of Richard's 14 1/2 years in prison under the Communist party of the Soviet Union and the underground church reveals the horrible consequence of an "impartial" purely godless style of government, where in reality the ruling party becomes the god. The atrocities I read on these pages will be burned into my mind for eternity. At the same time, the story of true love will overshadow those atrocities. The story of Jesus. The story of our brothers and sisters abroad, who we must strive with and support in their suffering while we sit comfortably in our recliners stressing over what kind of television we should purchase next. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14794400454448198744" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10178730805106566330">Not the best writing and disappointing from the standpoint that Wurmbrand unnecessarily refers to his fellow Catholic Christians as 'papists', and yet even so there is no denying his own suffering, devotion to Romanian Christians, the cause of Christianity worldwide and even the Communists who tortured him. Well worth reading. </span>

<div id="review_2124878204" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2124878204" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21724974-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506706341p2/21724974.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2124878204?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/21724974-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2124878204" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13007161874923687232">Richard Wurmbrand was a Romanian pastor who fought against the Christ-suppressing Communist regime of Eastern Europe's twentieth century. He was imprisoned for a total of fourteen years -- three of which he spent thirty feet underground without light or sound -- subjected to incredible physical torture and brainwashing. He never stopped witnessing about Jesus, his Lord and Saviour. He gave his heart to the Russians -- his fellow-prisoners and his captors -- and tried to bring them all to the kno</span>
  <span id="freeText13007161874923687232" style="display:none">Richard Wurmbrand was a Romanian pastor who fought against the Christ-suppressing Communist regime of Eastern Europe's twentieth century. He was imprisoned for a total of fourteen years -- three of which he spent thirty feet underground without light or sound -- subjected to incredible physical torture and brainwashing. He never stopped witnessing about Jesus, his Lord and Saviour. He gave his heart to the Russians -- his fellow-prisoners and his captors -- and tried to bring them all to the knowledge of Christ, the knowledge that brings eternal life and bliss.<br /><br /><b><i>Tortured for Christ</i> was a harrowing, uplifting and deeply challenging book.</b> The way Wurmbrand and other members of the Underground Church gave their lives to Jesus, in the face of unbelievable suffering, made me sit back with wide eyes. Wurmbrand could hardly walk a street without stopping someone to share with them the life-changing news of Jesus, even though doing so could (and did!) lead to his imprisonment. I live in a country of religious freedom and free speech, yet I hardly ever go out of my way to share the gospel.<br /><br /><i>"Persecution has always produced a better Christian -- a witnessing Christian, a soul-winning Christian. Communist persecution has backfired and produced serious, dedicated Christians such as are rarely seen in free lands. These people cannot understand how anyone can be a Christian and not want to win every soul they meet." (p116)</i><br /><br /><b>The West is dead and stagnant.</b> Our hearts are turning to stone -- we assume that no one will believe our message and so we are slow to witness, and the people we seek to reach are entrenched in our narcissistic, comfortable culture. Reading <i>Tortured for Christ</i> was like reading Acts; the stories of miraculous conversions! Whereas the West is like Israel at the crux of their idolatry, when there were no prophets, no sign of God's presence. The further we draw away from Him, the further He draws away from us.<br /><br />So this book was a huge challenge. One of the questions it asked was: <b>whom do you love? To which group of people will you give your heart?</b> For Wurmbrand, the answer was Communists and victims of Communism. For Hudson Taylor, it was the Chinese. For Dietrich Bonhoeffer, it was the victims of the Holocaust. <b>What about you? What about me?</b> You don't need to be a missionary abroad to live for Jesus; you don't need to be imprisoned and tortured like Richard Wurmbrand. But you do need to commit your life to making God known in your own world. In the West, where people do not know they need to be saved, this is harder than ever, <b>and so we must give our utmost.</b><br /><br /><i>"How then will they call on him in whom they have not believed? And how are they to believe in him of whom they have never heard? And how are they to hear without someone preaching? And how are they to preach unless they are sent? As it is written, 'How beautiful are the feet of those who preach the good news!'" (Romans 10:14-15)</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="13007161874923687232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2772528658" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2772528658" />
    <a title="Ebookwormy1" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1005834-ebookwormy1"><img alt="Ebookwormy1" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493483054p2/1005834.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2772528658?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ebookwormy1" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ebookwormy1" href="/user/show/1005834-ebookwormy1">Ebookwormy1</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1005834-ebookwormy1?shelf=z-2b-reviewed">z-2b-reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2772528658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18333383624204894009">Wurmbrand's autobiography tells how he went from Jew to Christian, and Marxist to Republican, under the Romanian governments of the Nazis and Communists. Wurmbrand and his family were brutalized, enslaved and imprisoned by the Communist government of Romania before he was ransomed by friends to become the voice of the persecuted Christian Church to the world. In 1966, he testified before the US Congress, famously removing his short to show the physical wounds of his torture. He was known as, "Th</span>
  <span id="freeText18333383624204894009" style="display:none">Wurmbrand's autobiography tells how he went from Jew to Christian, and Marxist to Republican, under the Romanian governments of the Nazis and Communists. Wurmbrand and his family were brutalized, enslaved and imprisoned by the Communist government of Romania before he was ransomed by friends to become the voice of the persecuted Christian Church to the world. In 1966, he testified before the US Congress, famously removing his short to show the physical wounds of his torture. He was known as, "The Voice of the Underground Church."<br /><br />Contemporary readers may be shocked to learn about the war between Communism/ Marxism and Christians, which has been largely sanitized today. Torture for Christ remains an important primary source account of this conflict. It also serves to illustrate how Statist governments control thei population and manipulate information, even as persecution continues today.<br /><br />Wurmbrand's work included 18 books of which Torture for Christ is probably the most influential. His advocacy culminated in founding an organization called Jesus to the Communist World. Recognizing Christians are increasingly facing persecution in non-Communist context (most notably the Muslim world), the organization incorporated Wurmbrand's designation and is today called The Voice of the Martyrs (VOM). VOM continues to advocate and report the challenges of persecuted Christians today. <br /><br />Torchlighters: Heroes of the Faith, Richard Wurmbrand, 2008<br />Available on DVD and onDemand for all ages. Includes both an animated account and a 50 minute documentary, as well as activities for children.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://torchlighters.org/heroes/richard-wurmbrand/">https://torchlighters.org/heroes/rich...</a><br /><br />See also his wife's story...<br />The Pastor's Wife, Sabrina Wurmbrand, 1970<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2772528392">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><br />For a glimpse of Romania after the Wurmbrand's are ransomed, see<br />Saving my Assassin, Prodan, 2016<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1667374287">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><br />For a theology of suffering developed by a Romanian, see<br />Suffering, Martyrdom and Rewards in Heaven, Ton, 2002<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20085195">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="18333383624204894009" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1804839675" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1804839675" />
    <a title="Michael O&#39;Brien" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9496879-michael-o-brien"><img alt="Michael O&#39;Brien" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548207742p2/9496879.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1804839675?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael O&#39;Brien" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael O&#39;Brien" href="/user/show/9496879-michael-o-brien">Michael O&#39;Brien</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1804839675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17292980071057100921">This is the story of Rev. Richard Wurmbrand, imprisoned for 14 years, by ruthless atheists in a repressive socialist state. It's more than just his story, but the story of many Christians who suffered terribly for their faith in Jesus Christ behind the Iron Curtain. I found it profoundly inspiring and relevant, especially since, increasingly, there is a growing hostility of Government officials and the national media in our own society against Christians. I found it had me wondering about how th</span>
  <span id="freeText17292980071057100921" style="display:none">This is the story of Rev. Richard Wurmbrand, imprisoned for 14 years, by ruthless atheists in a repressive socialist state. It's more than just his story, but the story of many Christians who suffered terribly for their faith in Jesus Christ behind the Iron Curtain. I found it profoundly inspiring and relevant, especially since, increasingly, there is a growing hostility of Government officials and the national media in our own society against Christians. I found it had me wondering about how the strength of the faith of us in the Free World compares with that of Christians who have suffered terribly under socialist and Islamist regimes. Sadly, I think that many would fall away -- which, initially, was the case in Romania during Wurmbrand's time when the atheists seized power there after World War 2. Interestingly, Wurmbrand showed the proper example for how the Underground Church overcame its oppressors --- not by violent resistance or by hatred --- but by having a love for Jesus Christ and a love for the souls of even the worst Communists and by having a unity and strength of purpose that the most churches in the Free World aspires to. Overall, an outstanding story of a Christian's strength under the most trying and dire of circumstances, one that I would recommend to anyone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17292980071057100921" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2626634842?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khari" href="/user/show/16880570-khari">Khari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780882643267" href="/book/show/1189251.Tortured_for_Christ">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16880570-khari?shelf=christian">christian</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2626634842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9239508144445252827">This was another excellent book.<br/><br/>This is now the second or third book I've read about people suffering under Communism because of their beliefs. <br/><br/>It's not as horrifying as the Gulag Archipelago was. Solznehitsyn focused on the horror of the tortures and life in Soviet prisons and prison camps. That wasn't Wurmbrand's focus at all. He gives only the barest description of what went on his prison sentence. <br/><br/>Instead he focused on the work God was doing inside of Communism, and it was powerful. It was p</span>
  <span id="freeText9239508144445252827" style="display:none">This was another excellent book.<br /><br />This is now the second or third book I've read about people suffering under Communism because of their beliefs. <br /><br />It's not as horrifying as the Gulag Archipelago was. Solznehitsyn focused on the horror of the tortures and life in Soviet prisons and prison camps. That wasn't Wurmbrand's focus at all. He gives only the barest description of what went on his prison sentence. <br /><br />Instead he focused on the work God was doing inside of Communism, and it was powerful. It was powerful to read about small children smuggling portions of the Bible to Russian soldiers. It was powerful to read of young women standing up to people who had the power to kill and maim them, but they never gave up on the truth. <br /><br />Perhaps the most astonishing thing to me was how these believers knew the word of God and put it into action. Even though most of them had never read the Bible in its entirety, they grasped its lessons and taught them to their fellow prisoners. That was something that really convicted me. I have read the bible through at least 3 times in my life, probably more like 10, but I don't recall how many times exactly, and yet there are still basic biblical truths I haven't grasped. I read some of the letters of Christians, one was from a girl named Nadia, she had only been a christian for a couple of months, and yet her letters were full of grace and scripture. She wasn't quoting scripture because she probably didn't have access to it, and yet she was still conveying its truth. It amazed me at what God is capable of doing in someone's life and shamed me because I still tend to keep my mouth shut about my beliefs.<br /><br />Deeply convicting book, very easy to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9239508144445252827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_540770668" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/540770668" />
    <a title="Clint Jackson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7318051-clint-jackson"><img alt="Clint Jackson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506913575p2/7318051.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/540770668?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clint Jackson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clint Jackson" href="/user/show/7318051-clint-jackson">Clint Jackson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer540770668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14019305888456406948">This book can be a painful book to read because of the things that the author, Richard Wurmbrand, went through. All the same, it is a powerful testament to the power of the Gospel and reveals the fact that persecution of the church continues on even to this day in the world. It also shows the power of the Spirit moving within people who TRULY believe in the Gospel. Many of these people had very little scripture. There was no complete book that contained the entire Bible or even an entire book of</span>
  <span id="freeText14019305888456406948" style="display:none">This book can be a painful book to read because of the things that the author, Richard Wurmbrand, went through. All the same, it is a powerful testament to the power of the Gospel and reveals the fact that persecution of the church continues on even to this day in the world. It also shows the power of the Spirit moving within people who TRULY believe in the Gospel. Many of these people had very little scripture. There was no complete book that contained the entire Bible or even an entire book of the Bible that was available to these people, yet they were more outspoken, more resilient, and more joyful than any Christian I have ever seen, and have only heard of such joy recorded in the Bible. There are people who would be baptized, and within months be at the maturity of a Christian that many Christians in the Western nations say takes years to attain. This book was written as a testament to the church in the West to aid their persecuted brothers in other lands. This book also serves as a testament on as to what happens when someone TRULY believes in the Gospel, and gives their lives over to the COMPLETE Lordship of Jesus Christ, and the fact that the only reason why pastors and preachers and Western Christians say that change within Christians is a slow, gradual process is because we've allowed people to believe that they don't have to give over everything of themselves to God. We've allowed people to believe a watered down Gospel. It's only true for someone so long as they give only parts of their life over to God. God changes you and moves within you as fast as you are willing to let him. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14019305888456406948" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3167684510" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3167684510" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14830128-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579058316p2/14830128.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3167684510?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/14830128-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3167684510" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1200523654691314440">I gave this a two star because I really did read it and finish it. I read it in that time when being ‘crucified for Christ,’ was a big deal. I also read ‘The Heavenly Man’ during that time, and comparing the two, this one comes out less appreciated. I respect Richard Wormbrand’s passion for what he chose to do with his life, but he also comes off rather entitled and egotistical. At one point close to the end of the book he dis-es the younger generation for ‘confirming to the world’ too much whil</span>
  <span id="freeText1200523654691314440" style="display:none">I gave this a two star because I really did read it and finish it. I read it in that time when being ‘crucified for Christ,’ was a big deal. I also read ‘The Heavenly Man’ during that time, and comparing the two, this one comes out less appreciated. I respect Richard Wormbrand’s passion for what he chose to do with his life, but he also comes off rather entitled and egotistical. At one point close to the end of the book he dis-es the younger generation for ‘confirming to the world’ too much while he only reluctantly participated. His words and perspectives are cutting. I can’t help but feel that though he has done much to respect and follow Jesus, he forgot the tenderness. In contrast, ‘The Heavenly Man’ is enduring. The character in that book endured similar persecution, but maintains the undying love. He holds the truth and beliefs of Jesus with tenderness and helps others with that same tenderness. The cutting remarks that he makes is that the church in the west persecuted each other much worse than the physical torture in China, simply by using words to tear each other down. I find that synopsis much easier to take because it’s true, and is said with regret and with the passion to pray for change. <br />So, I give this book a two. I appreciate reading of those who placed their life on the line in order to teach others of Jesus, but if you can’t come through the torture maintaining the love, I feel like something need to change. Wormbrand, I’m pretty sure, had a severe case of PTSD, and he wasn’t able to find a way to healing. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1200523654691314440" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText18429726395123772720" style="display:none">So difficult to read. Painful. As uncomfortable as it all is though, I don't want to go back to my ignorance of these things...blissfully living my self-absorbed, comfy life in Christ while around the world Christians are still suffering &amp; dying for their faith. <br /><br />A paragraph in a 1997 letter in the appendix from Frank R. Wolf, 10th district, Virginia, House of Representatives (on the subcommittee for Security &amp; Cooperation in Europe) hit me..."Worldwide persecution and martyrdom of Christians has increased and intensified to such an extent that more Christians have died for their faith in the 20th century than in all prior 19 centuries combined. Christian persecution did not dissipate with the fall of the Iron Curtain. Yet despite the fact it has persisted and accelerated, the persecution of Christians remains the great untold human rights story of this era." <br /><br />I now realize that, just because its not front page news, everything I had just read is still going on in earnest.   <span id="freeText6370519042778692430" style="display:none">This book is incredibly challenging and equally as encouraging.<br /> Wurmbrand uses his own experiences and those of other suffering believers to teach us about the nature of Communism and God’s ultimate victory. It isn’t a biography. Instead, it is a quick overview of the suffering of believers in the former Soviet Union, and a call to action to those of us who are free. It is also an explanation almost a mission statement of VOM.<br /> So many Christian organizations have believed the lie Communist offer, that this book could be a rude awakening for many. I would still recommend it to everyone. If you are saved, it will encourage you to examine your loyalties and look to God’s plan for your life. If you aren’t saved, it will show you the deep depravity man is capable of when he rejects God and the overwhelming love God shows those who accept Him. <br /> <br /></span>

Reading the problems these people had on an every day basis certainly put my own insignificant problems in perspective. <br /><br />Overall, this book brought me closer to God and I would highly recommend it to anyone.</span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124777927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3805108374345343085">As I read TORTURED FOR CHRIST I had many mixed feelings. I'll start with the what I loved about it. I can honestly say this book has changed me. Its challenged me to strive towards a heart that is ever thankful, praying and praising Almighty God without ceasing, regardless of circumstance. It's made me take a step back and examine my life and walk, and at the "persecution" I think I receive from unsaved family or friends. As an American Christian, born and raised on free soil, I don't know the f</span>
  <span id="freeText3805108374345343085" style="display:none">As I read TORTURED FOR CHRIST I had many mixed feelings. I'll start with the what I loved about it. I can honestly say this book has changed me. Its challenged me to strive towards a heart that is ever thankful, praying and praising Almighty God without ceasing, regardless of circumstance. It's made me take a step back and examine my life and walk, and at the "persecution" I think I receive from unsaved family or friends. As an American Christian, born and raised on free soil, I don't know the first thing about "persecution" - at least not compared to our steadfast brothers and sisters in captive nations. This book is a wake-up call to American Christians. I was deeply convicted reading what others have suffered for Jesus Christ, their attitude towards their torturers, and their unwavering love for God through it all.<br /><br />That being said, I have somewhat against this book. As I read TORTURED FOR CHRIST I kept feeling a check in my spirit... I finally realized it was because it's author has Catholic sympathies, even going so far, I feel, to endorse the Catholic Church. Now, please, I'm not saying any of this to out-do or make light of the suffering of those spoken of in this book. And I'm not saying it to start an argument and hurt the feelings of those who might read this review and not agree. I am not Catholic, but much of my extended family is. I love Catholics but I hate Catholicism. Why? Many reasons. Chiefly among them, is that MILLIONS of Protestant Christians were viciously tortured and brutally killed under the banner of Catholicism during the Popes Inquisition. The Dark Ages were the Dark Ages for this very reason; the popes made it so and not a single pope during or since has ever apologized for it.<br /><br />This book is titled "TORTURED FOR CHRIST" and both its title and contents speak of Christians suffering. That in mind, I find it odd and, frankly, disgustingly hypocritical that a man who is the "Voice of the Martyrs" could be so silent for the millions of souls martyred for the very organization he seems to endorse here. The Christians spoken of in this book suffered and died at the hands of godless people. The Christians during the Popes Inquisition suffered and died at the hands of those claiming to have God on their side.<br /><br />Believe me, I wanted to love this book; the whole book. I've heard nothing but praises for it and had it in my TBR pile for a while now, anxiously waiting to read it. It does have its good points, many in fact. It gripped my heart and had me crying more times that I can count. I took away invaluable witnessing material and was greatly convicted and challenged. But I simply cannot ignore or embrace Wurmbrand's obvious endorsement of the Catholic Church. I had to be a voice, however small, for my unsung brothers and sisters of centuries past who also suffered greatly for Christ. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3805108374345343085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_160541743" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160541743" />
    <a title="Luke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1452964-luke"><img alt="Luke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1219677952p2/1452964.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/160541743?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luke" href="/user/show/1452964-luke">Luke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer160541743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13515627084163229446">Just a fantastic, heart-breaking, and inspiring book. I can't believe I hadn't read this book before now, but I'm glad that I remedied the situation. This book was written by Pastor Richard Wurmbrand, a Romanian pastor who spent a total of 14 years in Communist prisons for daring to preach Christ under Communist rule. It is truly the work of a Spirit-filled believer who has had his faith tested and tried in the most oppressive conditions imaginable. Under conditions which would (and have) broken</span>
  <span id="freeText13515627084163229446" style="display:none">Just a fantastic, heart-breaking, and inspiring book. I can't believe I hadn't read this book before now, but I'm glad that I remedied the situation. This book was written by Pastor Richard Wurmbrand, a Romanian pastor who spent a total of 14 years in Communist prisons for daring to preach Christ under Communist rule. It is truly the work of a Spirit-filled believer who has had his faith tested and tried in the most oppressive conditions imaginable. Under conditions which would (and have) broken men for life, Pastor Wurmbrand recounts how the love of Christ and the Word of God shone more brightly, the darker their situation got. <br /><br />Similar to "The Hiding Place", what stands out for me is the thirst which these believers have for the Word and their Savior. It's hard for me to think of a more powerful witness to the truth of the Gospel than to read about the love which Wurmbrand and others bear for their tormentors. How even when they were being tortured endlessly, they cared more for the souls of their tormentors than for their own well-being. This unnatural love is simply impossible for the natural man.<br /><br />I knew about the Underground Church before reading this book, but it is heartening to hear stories about how it began and flourished under the Communists in Romania. I know that even now in 20+ places around the globe, fellow believers are suffering unimaginable deprivation for refusing to recant their belief in Christ. It truly serves to humble believers in the West who whine about "persecution" when we aren't allowed to say Merry Christmas during a school play. I recommend this book to any believer and also any non-believer who is interested to learn about the strength and grace of these saints in the face of savage and inhuman oppression. It is an uplifting story and one that helps to put your life into the proper perspective. The "prosperity gospel" is a shameful abomination on the face of Christendom and the fact that it hasn't been run out of town yet demonstrates that a lack of Biblical understanding coupled with pervasive materialism is more detrimental to the Church than unapologetic atheism.<br /><br />Thank you for taking the time to read my review.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13515627084163229446" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1007699975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6297052537047294920">"Tortured for Christ" is an amazing book about a pastor tortured by Communists in Romania. I like how the author warns about Communism infiltrating America. He gives examples of tortured people who have a joy that no person except themselves can truly understand. The people of the Underground Church have an immense love for the captors and those who've treated them cruelly. Bro. Wurmbrand shows the need for Christians in America to pray for people being persecuted, tortured, killed, and any comb</span>
  <span id="freeText6297052537047294920" style="display:none">"Tortured for Christ" is an amazing book about a pastor tortured by Communists in Romania. I like how the author warns about Communism infiltrating America. He gives examples of tortured people who have a joy that no person except themselves can truly understand. The people of the Underground Church have an immense love for the captors and those who've treated them cruelly. Bro. Wurmbrand shows the need for Christians in America to pray for people being persecuted, tortured, killed, and any combination of the three. He also shows us the effect that donating money to the cause can do. It is amazing how much these Christians can do with just one Bible. I hope that in the future, I will be able to help these works financially. Thanks, Bro Wurmbrand, for showing our churches just how bad things can get in a country without the freedom of religion.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NdXJqvZZuVwXBfQikoJdR8dRa8KAyMCbjQcD3nJ9qEMV4az2WGM0LNjR/yggbw4eCjol1epSGjZzNJosoVCyLw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Z2/CHRML8IZkqnLpYL/jHnheW1ereztKyPex7x5eSF9HW6dBvTF99qt+eePSUrBHtTUVQMHh4ec2xCgdzXNSMw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/44578.Richard_Wurmbrand">About Richard Wurmbrand</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/44578.Richard_Wurmbrand"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1501390657p3/44578.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/44578.Richard_Wurmbrand">Richard Wurmbrand
</a></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11126435085424995954">Early life<br/><br/>Richard Wurmbrand, the youngest of four boys, was born in 1909 in Bucharest in a Jewish family. He lived with his family in Istanbul for a short while; his father died when he was 9, and the Wurmbrands returned to Romania when he was 15.<br/><br/>As an adolescent, he became attracted to communism, and, after attending a series of illegal meetings of the Communist Party of Romania (PCdR), he was se</span>
  <span id="freeText11126435085424995954" style="display:none">Early life<br /><br />Richard Wurmbrand, the youngest of four boys, was born in 1909 in Bucharest in a Jewish family. He lived with his family in Istanbul for a short while; his father died when he was 9, and the Wurmbrands returned to Romania when he was 15.<br /><br />As an adolescent, he became attracted to communism, and, after attending a series of illegal meetings of the Communist Party of Romania (PCdR), he was sent to study Marxism in Moscow, but returned clandestinely the following year. Pursued by Siguranţa Statului (the secret police), he was arrested and held in Doftana prison. Wurmbrand subsequently renounced his political ideals.<br /><br />He married <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/376667.Sabina_Wurmbrand" rel="nofollow noopener">Sabina Oster</a> on October 26, 1936. Wurmbrand and his wife were converted to Christianity in 1938 through the witness of Christian Wolfkes, a Romanian Christian carpenter; they joined the Anglican Mission to the Jews. Wurmbrand was ordained twice - first as an Anglican, then, after World War II, as a Lutheran pastor.<br /><br />In 1944, when the Soviet Union occupied Romania as the first step to establishing the communist regime, Wurmbrand began a ministry to his Romanian countrymen and to the Red Army soldiers. When the government attempted to control the churches, he immediately began an "underground" ministry to his people. He was arrested on February 29, 1948, while on his way to church services.<br /><br />[edit] Prisons<br /><br />Wurmbrand, who passed through the penal facilities of Craiova, Gherla, the Danube-Black Sea Canal, Văcăreşti, Malmaison, Cluj, and ultimately Jilava, spent three years in solitary confinement. His wife, Sabina, was arrested in 1950 and spent three years of penal labour on the Canal.<br /><br />Pastor Wurmbrand was released in 1956, after eight and a half years, and, although warned not to preach, resumed his work in the underground church. He was arrested again in 1959, and sentenced to 25 years. During his imprisonment, he was beaten and tortured.<br /><br />Eventually, he was the recipient of an amnesty in 1964. Concerned with the possibility of further imprisonment, the Norwegian Mission to the Jews and the Hebrew Christian Alliance negotiated with the Communist authorities for his release from Romania for $10,000. He was convinced by underground church leaders to leave and become a voice for the persecuted church.<br /><br />[edit] Exile and mission<br /><br />Wurmbrand traveled to Norway, England, and then the United States. In May 1965, he testified in Washington, D.C. before the US Senate's Internal Security Subcommittee. He became known as the "The Voice of the Underground Church", doing much to publicize the persecution of Christians in Communist countries.<br /><br />In April 1967, the Wurmbrands formed Jesus To The Communist World (later named The Voice of the Martyrs), an interdenominational organization working initially with and for persecuted Christians in Communist countries, but later expanding its activities to help persecuted believers in other places, especially in the Muslim world. However, when in Namibia, and confronted with the case of Colin Winter, the Anglican Bishop of Namibia, who had supported African strikers and was eventually deported from Namibia by South Africa, Wurmbrand criticized the latter's anti-apartheid activism, and claimed resistance to communism was more important.<br /><br />In 1990 Richard and Sabina Wurmbrand returned to Romania for the first time in 25 years. The Voice of the Martyrs opened a printing facility and bookstore in Bucharest. He preached about God together with pastor Ioan Panican.<br /><br />The Wurmbrands had one son, Mihai. Wurmbrand wrote 18 books in English and others in Romanian. His best-known book is entitled Tortured for Christ, released in 1967. His wife, Sabina, died August 11, 2000.<br /><br />Pastor Wurmbrand died on February 17, 2001 in a hospital in Long Beach, California. His last address was in Palos Verdes, California. In 2006, he came fifth among the greatest Romanians according to the Mari Ro</span>
  <a data-text-id="11126435085424995954" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;It was strictly forbidden to preach to other prisoners. It was understood that whoever was caught doing this received a severe beating. A number of us decided to pay the price for the privilege of preaching, so we accepted their [the communists' ] terms. It was a deal; we preached and they beat us. We were happy preaching. They were happy beating us, so everyone was happy.&rdquo;</span>

They are spitting in His face." I said to her, "If I do so, you lose your husband." She replied, "I don't wish to have a coward as a husband.&rdquo;</span>
